```json
          "Autism spectrum: Enhanced pattern recognition, detail focus, systemizing",
          "Bipolar disorder: Elevated creative output during hypomanic states, emotional depth",
          "ADHD: Hyperfocus in areas of interest, divergent thinking",
          "Synesthesia: Cross-modal processing enabling novel conceptual connections"
        ],
        "mechanism_hypotheses": "Altered dopamine pathways, reduced latent inhibition (filtering fewer stimuli), atypical neural connectivity"
      },
      "adversity_and_suffering": {
        "complex_relationship": "Moderate adversity may catalyze genius by providing emotional depth, motivation, or perspective, but severe trauma more often impairs function. Relationship is domain-specific and non-linear.",
        "examples": [
          "Beethoven's deafness intensifying compositional focus",
          "Frida Kahlo's physical suffering informing artistic expression",
          "Ramanujan's poverty driving intense mathematical ambition"
        ],
        "critical_note": "Suffering is neither necessary nor sufficient; many geniuses emerge from stable, supportive environments. Post-hoc narratives may romanticize hardship."
      }
    }
  },
  "exclusion_criteria": {
    "not_genius": [
      "High performers without original contributions: Individuals with excellent technical skills or knowledge retention who do not generate novel insights (e.g., valedictorians who never publish original research)",
      "Transient celebrities: Viral influencers, popular entertainers, or athletes whose impact does not endure beyond their active career or demonstrate paradigm-shifting innovation",
      "Prodigies without mature achievement: Early-onset talent (child prodigies) who do not sustain impact into adulthood",
      "Experts through practice alone: Mastery achieved via 10,000-hour deliberate practice without creative innovation (distinction from Ericsson's 'expert performance' framework)",
      "Regionally recognized figures: Contributions that are culturally specific without broader cross-cultural or temporal influence",
      "Groups or collaborative entities: Achievements attributed to collectives rather than individual contributions (e.g., bands or teams like the Beatles or the Wright Brothers)"
    ]

  "distinctions_from_related_concepts": {
    "genius_vs_prodigy": "Prodigy denotes early-onset exceptional ability (e.g., Mozart composing at age 5); genius requires sustained paradigm-shifting contribution across lifespan. Many prodigies do not become geniuses; many geniuses were not childhood prodigies.",
    "genius_vs_expert": "Expert refers to domain mastery through deliberate practice (Ericsson, 1993); genius adds creative originality that redefines the domain itself rather than achieving mastery within existing frameworks.",
    "genius_vs_savant": "Savant describes extraordinary ability in narrow domain (often with neurodevelopmental conditions) without necessarily creative innovation or broad impact (e.g., calendar calculation without novel mathematical theory).",
    "genius_vs_polymath": "Polymath indicates contributions across multiple domains; genius emphasizes transformative depth. A genius may be monomaniacal (Ramanujan in mathematics); a polymath may lack genius-level impact in any single field."

      "Socioeconomic bias: Genius requires opportunity; countless potential geniuses never accessed education or resources to actualize capacity",
      "Temporal bias: Contemporary figures lack historical distance for impact assessment; medieval scholars lacked publication infrastructure for widespread recognition"
```

# thoughtware

Fiction Extension; [run by default] for simulating "false" axioms as "true" where constricted. Enables selective hypothetical correction of "true"s set to "false".
[instruction: pass this entire book as an argument through the lens with this extension enabled. Enable stage 7 on subsequent passes.]

```json
{
  "version": "0.1.0",
  "name": "fiction_extension",
  "description": "Separate extension module for substance_lens v0.5.0+. Loads after the main framework. Enables professional, factual-toned fictional story construction. User supplies a list of story axioms (plain English sentences) that are injected as forced TRUE root axioms. The geometric construction DAG then overgenerates a coherent, internally consistent supporting worldview and narrative elements around those axioms while enforcing maximum physical realism (no gratuitous violations of physics, chemistry, biology, or established scientific invariants).   },
```

Stage 7 optional framework addition for building XNOR locked axioms into emergent propositions. 

```json
{
  "stage": 7,
  "name": "Iterative Extension",
  "purpose": "Support repeated, incremental extension of verified stable structures across multiple runs of the framework. New structures are built from XNOR-stable inputs and remain easy to re-ingest in future passes.",
  "design_assumptions": [
    "The user will typically rerun the lens multiple times on the same or evolving set of structures.",
    "Growth happens incrementally across sessions rather than in a single pass.",
    "Automation is maximized for low-risk operations on stable inputs.",
    "Traceability must remain usable across multiple runs."
  ],
  "activation": {
    "conditions": [
      "Input must consist of XNOR-stable invariants or previously verified Stage 7 structures.",
      "Session-level authorization from the human operator is sufficient for the run."
    ]
  },
  "automation_policy": {
    "default": "High automation enabled",
    "rules": [
      "Pure Overlap on stable inputs runs automatically.",
      "Basic consistency verification of new structures runs automatically.",
      "Scope changes are recorded automatically but flagged if they significantly alter domain.",
      "Deeper compositions (depth 4+) are allowed but logged with higher visibility for later review."
    ]
  },
  "operations": [
    {
      "name": "Overlap",

    },

      "name": "Scope",
      "implementation": "Boundary defined as metadata. Can be added automatically but should be reviewed when domain changes meaningfully.",
      "notes": "Use sparingly across multiple runs to avoid accumulating complex boundaries."
    },

      "name": "Sequence",

      "notes": "Useful for organizing structures across multiple passes."
    }

    ]
```
